{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01HZV7VUC3DWpR3zKguS2ZaT","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01JeF9jkKjryt7GxpVN9ytyC","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Istio Pilot Discovery Service Architecture\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nIstio Pilot's Discovery Service is the control plane component that translates high-level mesh configuration (VirtualServices, DestinationRules, etc.) into Envoy-specific xDS (Envoy Discovery Service) resources. It serves a bidirectional gRPC stream to each connected proxy, allowing Pilot to push configuration updates in real-time while proxies request specific resources. The service integrates with multiple service registries (Kubernetes, ServiceEntry, external services), supports multi-cluster deployments, and efficiently manages thousands of concurrent proxy connections.\n\nThis document explains the four primary subsystems that work together to implement this functionality:\n\n1. **DiscoveryServer** — The gRPC server implementing Envoy's xDS v3 protocol\n2. **ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service)** — The bidirectional stream handler and connection model\n3. **PushContext** — The immutable configuration snapshot used during each push\n4. **ServiceRegistry** — The service discovery layer feeding the DiscoveryServer\n\n---\n\n## 1. DiscoveryServer — The xDS gRPC Server\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe `DiscoveryServer` (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:64`) is the central gRPC service that implements Envoy's xDS v3 protocol. It manages all active proxy connections, coordinates configuration pushes across the fleet, implements request-rate limiting, and maintains caches of generated xDS resources.\n\n### Architecture\n\n**Core Fields** (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:65-138`):\n\n- **`Env *model.Environment`** — The cluster's configuration state, including:\n  - `ServiceDiscovery` — The service registry interface\n  - `ConfigStore` — Istio's CRD store (VirtualServices, DestinationRules, etc.)\n  - `Cache` — The xDS resource cache\n  - `pushContext` — The current mesh-wide configuration snapshot\n\n- **`adsClients map[string]*Connection`** — Tracks all active proxy connections, keyed by proxy ID. Each connection wraps a bidirectional gRPC stream with proxy metadata. This map is the single source of truth for which proxies are connected.\n\n- **`Generators map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator`** — Maps generator types to custom implementations. Users extend Pilot by registering custom generators for resource types. Each generator implements the `XdsResourceGenerator` interface to produce resource-specific outputs (Clusters, Listeners, Routes, etc.).\n\n- **`pushChannel chan *model.PushRequest`** — A buffered channel (size 10) that debounces rapid configuration changes. When a config event arrives (e.g., ServiceEntry created, VirtualService modified), it's sent to this channel.\n\n- **`pushQueue *PushQueue`** — A queue that accepts debounced push requests and distributes them to proxies. Provides throttling via `concurrentPushLimit`.\n\n- **`concurrentPushLimit chan struct{}`** — A semaphore (size controlled by `PushThrottle` feature flag) that limits concurrent xDS pushes to prevent overwhelming the system.\n\n- **`RequestRateLimit *rate.Limiter`** — Per-request rate limiting to prevent thundering herd of incoming requests from proxies.\n\n- **`Cache model.XdsCache`** — Stores computed xDS resources (clusters, listeners, routes, secrets). Can be disabled if caching is not desired.\n\n### Request Processing Pipeline\n\n#### 1. **Initialization and Registration**\n\nWhen Pilot starts, `NewDiscoveryServer()` (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:141`) creates a `DiscoveryServer` and initializes:\n\n- Empty `adsClients` map for tracking connections\n- Debounce channels and push queues\n- Configuration watchers for config and service registry changes\n\nThe server registers itself with the gRPC server via `Register()` (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:197`), which calls:\n```go\ndiscovery.RegisterAggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer(rpcs, s)\n```\n\n#### 2. **Push Triggering and Debouncing**\n\nWhen any Istio configuration or service registry state changes:\n\n1. **`ConfigUpdate()`** (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`, line 276) is called with a `PushRequest` containing:\n   - `Full bool` — Whether to recompute the entire push context\n   - `ConfigsUpdated sets.Set[ConfigKey]` — Specific configurations that changed (optimization)\n   - `Reason ReasonStats` — Debugging reason (e.g., \"ServiceEntryCreated\", \"EndpointsUpdated\")\n\n2. The request enters `pushChannel` for debouncing in `handleUpdates()` (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:326`), which:\n   - Waits for a quiet period (`DebounceAfter`) without new changes\n   - Coalesces multiple changes into a single push\n   - Enforces maximum wait time (`debounceMax`)\n\n3. **`Push()`** (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:258`) is called with the debounced request:\n   - If full push, `initPushContext()` recomputes the entire mesh state\n   - Updates `CommittedUpdates` counter\n   - Enqueues the request in `pushQueue` for distribution to proxies\n\n#### 3. **Cache Management**\n\nThe `Cache` field implements the `model.XdsCache` interface, storing computed resources keyed by:\n- Proxy metadata (region, cluster, node type)\n- Resource type (Cluster, Listener, Route, etc.)\n- Configuration version\n\n**Cache Invalidation** (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:246`):\n- `dropCacheForRequest()` clears the cache when configuration changes\n- If a push is `Full`, the entire cache is cleared\n- If incremental, only affected resource types are invalidated\n\n---\n\n## 2. ADS and the Connection Model\n\n### Overview\n\nThe Aggregated Discovery Service (ADS) in `ads.go` implements the bidirectional gRPC streaming protocol that connects Pilot to Envoy proxies. A single `Stream()` handler manages the lifecycle of each proxy connection and coordinates configuration push/pull interactions.\n\n### Connection Lifecycle\n\n#### The `Connection` Type (`pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go:71-88`)\n\nEach connected proxy is represented by a `Connection` struct:\n\n```go\ntype Connection struct {\n    xds.Connection           // Embedded base with stream and peer address\n    node *core.Node          // Original Envoy node metadata\n    proxy *model.Proxy       // Parsed proxy metadata (cluster, namespace, etc.)\n    deltaStream ...          // For Delta XDS (incremental)\n    s *DiscoveryServer       // Reference to parent server\n    ids []string             // Identity certificates from mTLS\n}\n```\n\nKey responsibilities:\n- **Wraps the gRPC stream** — Holds the `DiscoveryStream` for bidirectional communication\n- **Stores proxy metadata** — Extracts and caches information from Envoy's node metadata (cluster ID, pod name, namespace, etc.)\n- **Tracks state** — Maintains resource versions, watched resources, and last push time\n\n#### Establishing a Connection: `Stream()` (`pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go:188-235`)\n\n1. **Server Readiness Check** — Returns `Unavailable` if caches not synced; prevents connecting proxies from getting empty config\n2. **Authentication** (`ads.go:220-228`) — Validates mTLS/authentication credentials\n3. **Rate Limiting** (`ads.go:215`) — Enforces per-request rate limit using token bucket\n4. **Context Initialization** (`ads.go:231`):\n   ```go\n   s.globalPushContext().InitContext(s.Env, nil, nil)\n   ```\n   This ensures the global push context is populated. Happens once; subsequent calls return immediately.\n5. **Connection Creation** (`ads.go:232-234`):\n   - Creates a new `Connection` struct wrapping the stream\n   - Sets parent reference `con.s = s`\n   - Delegates to `xds.Stream()` for stream handling\n6. **Proxy Initialization** in `initConnection()` (`ads.go:240`):\n   - Parses node metadata into a `Proxy` object\n   - Registers the connection in `adsClients` map\n   - Initializes proxy-specific state (sidecar scope, watched resources)\n\n### Request Processing: `processRequest()` (`ads.go:139-181`)\n\nWhen an Envoy proxy sends a `DiscoveryRequest`:\n\n1. **Deduplication Check** — `xds.ShouldRespond()` determines if a response is needed based on:\n   - Previous version (already sent to this proxy)\n   - Nonce (preventing duplicate ACKs)\n\n2. **Configuration Preparation** — Constructs a `PushRequest` with:\n   - The proxy's last known `PushContext` (to avoid re-initializing)\n   - `Full: true` for immediate response (not waiting for debouncing)\n   - Last push time (used by cache for staleness detection)\n\n3. **Sidecar Scope Validation** (`ads.go:173-179`) — If the proxy's sidecar scope version doesn't match the push context version, `computeProxyState()` recomputes it\n\n4. **Response Generation** — Calls `pushXds()` to generate and send the response via the appropriate generator\n\n### Push Coordination: `pushConnection()` (`ads.go`, line not shown but referenced)\n\nWhen Pilot needs to push configuration to a specific connection:\n\n1. Gets the `Generator` for the proxy type (sidecar, gateway, waypoint)\n2. Calls `Generator.Generate()` to produce xDS resources for the proxy\n3. Sends a `DiscoveryResponse` via the stream\n4. Updates metrics and error tracking\n\n### Delta XDS: `DeltaAggregatedResources()` (`ads.go:467`)\n\nFor incremental updates, Envoy can use Delta XDS to receive only changed resources:\n\n1. **Incremental Resources** — Only resources that changed are sent\n2. **Deleted Resources** — Resource names that should be removed are sent\n3. **State Tracking** — The client tracks subscribed resources and version numbers\n\nThis reduces bandwidth for large clusters with frequent endpoint updates.\n\n---\n\n## 3. PushContext — Configuration Snapshot and Translation\n\n### Purpose\n\nA `PushContext` is an **immutable snapshot of the entire mesh configuration** used during a single push. It's created when configuration changes and shared across all proxies during that push, ensuring consistency. It also serves as the translation engine that converts Istio's high-level configuration into Envoy-specific resources.\n\nLocated in: `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:207-280`\n\n### Architecture\n\n#### Core Indexes\n\nA `PushContext` maintains several in-memory indexes for fast lookups:\n\n1. **`ServiceIndex serviceIndex`** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:65-91`) — Indexes all services by visibility:\n   - `public` — Services with `exportTo: \"*\"` (visible across the mesh)\n   - `privateByNamespace` — Services with `exportTo: \".\"` (visible only within namespace)\n   - `exportedToNamespace` — Services exported to specific namespaces\n   - `HostnameAndNamespace` — Services keyed by hostname and namespace\n   - `instancesByPort` — Cached endpoint lookups by port\n\n   **Usage**: When generating CDS (Cluster Discovery Service), Pilot looks up services this index determines which proxies can see which services.\n\n2. **`virtualServiceIndex virtualServiceIndex`** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:100-116`) — Indexes VirtualServices by visibility:\n   - `publicByGateway` — Public VirtualServices by gateway\n   - `privateByNamespaceAndGateway` — Namespace-local VirtualServices\n   - `delegates` — Delegates in VirtualService hierarchies\n   - `referencedDestinations` — Services referenced by VirtualServices\n\n   **Usage**: When generating RDS (Route Discovery Service), Pilot looks up VirtualServices to build HTTP routes.\n\n3. **`destinationRuleIndex destinationRuleIndex`** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:132-146`) — Indexes DestinationRules:\n   - `namespaceLocal` — DestinationRules per namespace\n   - `exportedByNamespace` — Exported DestinationRules\n   - `specificDestRules` and `wildcardDestRules` — Organized by target host\n\n   **Usage**: When generating clusters, DestinationRules are consulted for load balancing policies, connection pools, and traffic policies.\n\n4. **`sidecarIndex sidecarIndex`** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:148-180`) — Stores Sidecar configurations:\n   - `sidecarsByNamespace` — User-defined sidecars per namespace\n   - `meshRootSidecarConfig` — Root namespace sidecar (defaults for whole mesh)\n   - `defaultSidecarsByNamespace` — Computed defaults if no sidecar defined\n\n   **Usage**: Sidecars define which services a proxy can see. When computing routes and clusters for a proxy, the sidecar scope limits what's included.\n\n5. **`gatewayIndex gatewayIndex`** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:182-195`) — Indexes Gateway resources by namespace and globally.\n\n6. **`virtualServiceIndex.delegates`** — Maps root VirtualServices to their delegates, used for hierarchical route computation.\n\n#### Metrics and Status Tracking\n\n- **`ProxyStatus map[string]map[string]ProxyPushStatus`** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:211`) — Tracks push errors per proxy per error code, used for debugging and metrics\n- **`serviceAccounts map[serviceAccountKey][]string`** — Maps services to their service accounts for RBAC\n\n#### Configuration Objects\n\nA `PushContext` also holds:\n\n- **`Mesh *meshconfig.MeshConfig`** — Global mesh configuration\n- **`JwtKeyResolver *model.JwksResolver`** — JWT public key resolver for authentication policies\n- **`AuthnPolicies *AuthenticationPolicies`** — Authentication policies in the mesh\n- **`AuthzPolicies *AuthorizationPolicies`** — Authorization (RBAC) policies\n- **`Telemetry *Telemetries`** — Telemetry policies\n- **`ProxyConfigs *ProxyConfigs`** — Per-proxy configuration overrides\n- **`Networks *meshconfig.MeshNetworks`** — Multi-cluster network topology\n\n### PushContext Lifecycle\n\n#### Creation: `NewPushContext()` (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:735`)\n\nCreates a new, empty `PushContext` with initialized but empty indexes.\n\n#### Initialization: `InitContext()` (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`, method)\n\nCalled when configuration changes to populate the indexes:\n\n1. **Rebuilds all indexes** from the current `ConfigStore`:\n   - Scans all Services and builds `ServiceIndex`\n   - Scans all VirtualServices and builds `virtualServiceIndex`\n   - Scans all DestinationRules and indexes them\n   - Indexes Sidecars, Gateways, EnvoyFilters, etc.\n\n2. **Applies visibility rules** based on `exportTo`:\n   - Services/routing rules with `exportTo: \"*\"` go into `public`\n   - `exportTo: \".\"` goes into `privateByNamespace`\n   - Explicit namespace exports are indexed separately\n\n3. **Computes derived state**:\n   - Merges DestinationRules for the same host\n   - Validates configurations and logs errors\n   - Caches endpoint lookups for frequently accessed services\n\n4. **Thread-safety**: Protected by `initializeMutex`; multiple concurrent calls return immediately after first initialization\n\n**Performance Note**: `InitContext()` is expensive (scans all CRDs, indexes them) and happens only when configuration changes (debounced). This is why it's debounced; calling it on every request would be prohibitively expensive.\n\n### Configuration Translation: From Istio to Envoy\n\nThe `PushContext` serves as the input to resource generators that translate Istio's configuration into Envoy resources. The translation happens in `pilot/pkg/networking/core/` and uses the indexes in `PushContext`.\n\n#### Example: VirtualService → Route\n\n1. **Input**: A `VirtualService` specifying:\n   ```yaml\n   apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3\n   kind: VirtualService\n   metadata:\n     name: bookinfo\n   spec:\n     hosts:\n     - bookinfo.example.com\n     http:\n     - match:\n       - uri:\n           prefix: /reviews\n       route:\n       - destination:\n           host: reviews\n           port:\n             number: 8080\n           subset: v1\n   ```\n\n2. **Generator Lookup**:\n   - RDS generator (`pilot/pkg/xds/rds.go`) is invoked for the requesting proxy\n   - Looks up `bookinfo.example.com` in `virtualServiceIndex.publicByGateway`\n   - Retrieves the `VirtualService` spec\n\n3. **Route Computation** (`pilot/pkg/networking/core/route/`):\n   - Builds an Envoy `RouteConfiguration` with:\n     - Route match conditions (URI prefix)\n     - Route actions (forward to `reviews` cluster)\n     - Weights, retries, timeouts from the VirtualService spec\n\n4. **DestinationRule Application**:\n   - Looks up `reviews` in `destinationRuleIndex`\n   - If a `DestinationRule` exists for `reviews`, applies:\n     - Load balancing policy (round-robin, least request, etc.)\n     - Connection pool settings\n     - Outlier detection\n\n5. **Output**: An Envoy `RouteConfiguration` with fully populated route actions\n\n#### Example: Service + DestinationRule → Cluster\n\n1. **Input**: A Kubernetes Service `reviews.default.svc.cluster.local` and optional `DestinationRule`\n\n2. **Cluster Generation** (`pilot/pkg/xds/cds.go`, `pilot/pkg/networking/core/cluster_builder.go`):\n   - Looks up the service in `ServiceIndex.public` or `privateByNamespace`\n   - Creates an Envoy Cluster with:\n     - Service name as cluster name\n     - Virtual IP (from ClusterVIPs) or DNS resolution mode\n     - Service ports\n\n3. **DestinationRule Enhancements**:\n   - Looks up `DestinationRule` for the service in `destinationRuleIndex`\n   - If subsets are defined, creates subset-specific clusters (e.g., `reviews-v1`, `reviews-v2`)\n   - Applies load balancing, connection pools, outlier detection\n\n4. **Endpoint Resolution** (EDS — Endpoint Discovery Service):\n   - **Full CDS**: Cluster points to EDS (dynamic endpoint discovery)\n   - **EDS**: Endpoints are fetched from service registry, filtered by:\n     - Health status (Ready pods only)\n     - Sidecar scope visibility\n     - Network locality (for multi-cluster routing)\n\n### Shared State During Push\n\nDuring a single push:\n- All proxies see the same `PushContext` snapshot\n- All resource generators use the same indexes\n- If config changes mid-push, they're debounced and handled in the next push\n\nThis guarantees **consistency** — a proxy won't receive partially updated configuration that doesn't match other proxies' views.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe service registry feeds the discovery service with information about available services and their endpoints. It's abstracted via the `ServiceDiscovery` interface (`pilot/pkg/model/service.go:899`), allowing multiple implementations for Kubernetes, ServiceEntry, external registries, and aggregation across clusters.\n\n### ServiceDiscovery Interface (`pilot/pkg/model/service.go:899`)\n\nThe interface defines:\n\n```go\ntype ServiceDiscovery interface {\n    Services() []*Service\n    GetService(hostname host.Name) *Service\n    GetProxyServiceTargets(proxy *model.Proxy) []model.ServiceTarget\n    InstancesByPort(svc *Service, port int, labels labels.Collection) []*model.IstioEndpoint\n    GetNetworkGateway(network string) *model.NetworkGateway\n    // ... and other methods\n}\n```\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- **`Services()`** — Returns all services in the registry\n- **`GetService(hostname)`** — Looks up a service by FQDN\n- **`InstancesByPort()`** — Gets endpoints for a service on a specific port, optionally filtered by labels\n- **`GetProxyServiceTargets()`** — Returns services co-located with a proxy (for multi-cluster routing)\n\n### Kubernetes Service Registry\n\nThe Kubernetes implementation in `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/` watches Kubernetes API objects:\n\n#### Watched Resources:\n\n1. **Services** (`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go`):\n   - Each Kubernetes Service becomes an Istio Service\n   - Hostname: `<name>.<namespace>.svc.cluster.local`\n   - Ports, ClusterIP, and labels are extracted\n\n2. **EndpointSlices** (`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/endpointslice.go`):\n   - Kubernetes 1.19+ uses EndpointSlices instead of Endpoints\n   - Each slice contains a subset of endpoints for a service\n   - Pilot aggregates slices and watches for changes\n\n3. **Pods** (`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/pod.go`):\n   - Watches pod creation/deletion to track endpoint health\n   - Used for determining which endpoints are \"Ready\"\n   - Feeds into the EndpointIndex for EDS\n\n4. **Nodes** (`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/network.go`):\n   - Watches node labels for region/zone topology\n   - Used for locality-aware load balancing\n\n#### Service Registry Flow:\n\n```\nKubernetes API\n    ↓\nService/Endpoint Watchers\n    ↓\nEndpointIndex (pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go)\n    ↓\nProxyUpdate() [notifies xDS server]\n    ↓\nDiscoveryServer.ConfigUpdate()\n    ↓\nPush to all proxies\n```\n\nWhen a pod is added/removed:\n1. EndpointSlice changes → detected by watcher\n2. `ProxyUpdate()` is called → triggers EDS push\n3. Pilot computes endpoint list and sends EDS update to proxies\n4. Proxies update their load balancers\n\n### ServiceEntry Registry\n\n`ServiceEntry` CRDs allow declaring external services:\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3\nkind: ServiceEntry\nmetadata:\n  name: external-db\nspec:\n  hosts:\n  - db.external.example.com\n  ports:\n  - port: 5432\n    protocol: TCP\n  resolution: STATIC\n  endpoints:\n  - address: 192.168.1.1\n```\n\nThe `serviceentry` registry provider converts these into Istio Service objects, allowing them to be treated like Kubernetes services for routing purposes.\n\n### Aggregate Controller (Multi-Cluster)\n\nThe aggregate controller in `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/` combines multiple service registries:\n\n```\nKubernetes Cluster 1\n    ↓\nKubernetes Registry\n    ↓\n        → Aggregate Controller → Combined view\n        ↓\nKubernetes Cluster 2\n    ↓\nKubernetes Registry + ServiceEntry\n```\n\n**Multi-Cluster Logic**:\n\n1. **Local Services** — From the local cluster's Kubernetes registry\n2. **Remote Services** — From other clusters (via `ServiceImport` CRDs or direct watches)\n3. **ServiceEntry Services** — Defined via Istio CRDs\n\nAll are aggregated into a single `ServiceDiscovery` interface. A proxy in Cluster 1 can access services from Cluster 2 if they're exported via:\n- Kubernetes `ServiceExport` CRD\n- Istio `exportTo` rules\n- Multi-cluster networking configuration\n\n#### Cross-Cluster Routing:\n\nWhen a proxy in Cluster 1 needs to reach a service in Cluster 2:\n\n1. Service discovered via aggregate registry (Cluster 2's service)\n2. CDS includes endpoints from Cluster 2\n3. Endpoints include the cross-cluster gateway IP (from `NetworkManager`)\n4. Traffic is routed through the gateway (via mTLS or HBONE in ambient mode)\n\n### Endpoint Index: Efficient Endpoint Lookups\n\nThe `EndpointIndex` in `pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go` maintains efficient endpoint lookups:\n\n- **Organized by Service Key** — `namespace/hostname`\n- **Sharded by Endpoint IP** — Allows for incremental updates (when pod scales, only affected shard updates)\n- **Cached InstancesByPort Results** — Frequently accessed endpoint lookups are cached\n\n**Usage in EDS**:\n\n```\nEDS Request (what endpoints for service X?)\n    ↓\nEndpointIndex.InstancesByPort(service X, port 8080)\n    ↓\nReturns endpoints filtered by:\n   - Health status (Ready pods only)\n   - Labels (if specified in DestinationRule subset)\n   - Network locality (for locality-aware load balancing)\n```\n\n### Triggering Pushes from Service Registry\n\nWhen service state changes:\n\n1. **Endpoint Change** (pod added/removed):\n   - Triggers EDS (Endpoint Discovery Service) push (not full push)\n   - Reason: `EndpointUpdate`\n   - Only clusters referencing that service are updated\n\n2. **Service Change** (service created/deleted):\n   - Triggers full CDS (Cluster Discovery Service) push\n   - Also triggers LDS/RDS (listeners and routes may reference new service)\n   - Reason: `ServiceUpdate`\n\n3. **Debouncing**:\n   - Multiple endpoint changes are debounced (if `EnableEDSDebounce` is true)\n   - Avoids flapping when many pods scale simultaneously\n\n### Multi-Cluster Failure Handling\n\nIf a remote cluster becomes unavailable:\n\n1. **Service discovery removes remote services** from the aggregate view\n2. **Proxies are updated** via a config push\n3. **Routes referencing removed services** are pruned\n4. **Clients get connection errors** (graceful degradation)\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: From Configuration Change to Proxy Update\n\n### Complete Example: VirtualService Creation\n\n```\n1. User creates VirtualService CRD in Kubernetes\n   ↓\n2. Kubernetes API notifies ConfigStore watcher\n   ↓\n3. ConfigStore calls ConfigUpdate() with:\n   {Full: true, ConfigsUpdated: {VirtualService/namespace/name}, Reason: ConfigUpdate}\n   ↓\n4. ConfigUpdate() sends to pushChannel\n   ↓\n5. handleUpdates() debounces (waits for quiet period or max delay)\n   ↓\n6. Push() is called:\n   a. initPushContext() rescans all CRDs, rebuilds indexes\n   b. Calls computeProxyState() for each connected proxy (if needed)\n   c. Enqueues PushRequest in pushQueue\n   ↓\n7. sendPushes() distributes:\n   a. Acquires concurrentPushLimit semaphore\n   b. Iterates over adsClients (all connected proxies)\n   c. For each proxy, calls pushConnection()\n   ↓\n8. For each proxy, resource generators create Envoy config:\n   a. RDS generator uses virtualServiceIndex to build routes\n   b. CDS generator uses ServiceIndex to build clusters\n   c. Generators apply DestinationRules, EnvoyFilters, etc.\n   ↓\n9. xDS responses are sent to proxies via gRPC stream\n   ↓\n10. Proxies acknowledge with DiscoveryRequest (ACK/NACK)\n    ↓\n11. Errors tracked in ProxyStatus for debugging\n```\n\n### Complete Example: Pod Scale Event\n\n```\n1. Pod is added in Kubernetes\n   ↓\n2. EndpointSlice watcher detects change\n   ↓\n3. EndpointIndex is updated with new endpoint IP\n   ↓\n4. EndpointIndex calls ProxyUpdate() via callback\n   ↓\n5. ProxyUpdate() calls ConfigUpdate() with:\n   {Full: false, Reason: EndpointUpdate}\n   ↓\n6. (Same debounce → push → xDS flow)\n   ↓\n7. EDS generator reads EndpointIndex for affected service\n   ↓\n8. EDS update sent to proxies referencing the service\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\n### 1. Custom Resource Generators\n\nUsers can extend Istio by registering custom generators for any xDS resource type:\n\n```go\ngenerator := &myCustomGenerator{}\ndiscoveryServer.Generators[\"my-generator-type\"] = generator\n```\n\nGenerators implement the `XdsResourceGenerator` interface:\n- `Generate()` — Called to produce resources for a proxy\n- `GenerateDelta()` — Called for delta/incremental updates\n\n**Use Cases**:\n- Custom cluster discovery from external systems\n- Custom route generation based on external rules\n- Custom secret generation from external PKI\n\n### 2. Custom Configuration Types\n\nVia the `ConfigStore` interface, custom CRD types can be added. Pilot will:\n- Watch the new type\n- Include it in `InitContext()` rebuilding\n- Trigger pushes when instances change\n\n**Use Cases**:\n- Custom traffic policies\n- Custom observability configurations\n- Custom security rules\n\n### 3. EnvoyFilter\n\nEnvoyFilter CRDs in `pilot/pkg/networking/core/envoyfilter/` allow patching generated Envoy config:\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3\nkind: EnvoyFilter\nmetadata:\n  name: add-custom-header\nspec:\n  workloadSelector:\n    labels:\n      app: httpbin\n  configPatches:\n  - applyTo: HTTP_FILTER\n    patch:\n      operation: INSERT_BEFORE\n      value:\n        name: custom-header-filter\n        typed_config:\n          \"@type\": ...\n```\n\nEnvoyFilters are indexed in `PushContext.envoyFiltersByNamespace` and applied during resource generation.\n\n### 4. External Service Registries\n\nCustom `ServiceDiscovery` implementations can be registered:\n\n```go\ncustomRegistry := NewCustomServiceRegistry()\naggregate.Controller.AddRegistry(customRegistry)\n```\n\nAllows integrating with:\n- Consul\n- Eureka\n- Custom APIs\n- Cloud provider service catalogs\n\n### 5. Request Hooks\n\nProxyNeedsPush (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:78`) allows filtering which proxies get pushed:\n\n```go\ndiscoveryServer.ProxyNeedsPush = func(proxy *model.Proxy, req *model.PushRequest) (*model.PushRequest, bool) {\n    if shouldSkip(proxy) {\n        return nil, false  // Skip this proxy\n    }\n    return req, true\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases**:\n- Route updates only to affected proxies\n- Skip proxies in specific conditions\n- Custom push logic\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### 1. Configuration Validation Errors\n\nWhen `InitContext()` processes configurations:\n- Invalid CRDs are logged, not propagated\n- `PushContext.ProxyStatus` tracks errors per proxy\n- Proxies continue with last-known-good configuration\n\n**Recovery**: Fix the CRD and push again.\n\n### 2. Push Failures\n\nIf an error occurs while pushing to a proxy:\n- Tracked in `ProxyStatus[proxyID][errorCode]`\n- Exposed via `/debug/push_status` endpoint\n- Next `ConfigUpdate()` will retry\n\n**Common causes**:\n- Network errors (transient)\n- Stream closed (proxy disconnected)\n- Resource generation failure (bug)\n\n### 3. Proxy Connection Failures\n\nIf a proxy disconnects:\n- Connection is removed from `adsClients`\n- Next connection reconnects and gets full config\n- No special recovery needed\n\n### 4. Resource Generation Panics\n\nGenerators that panic are caught:\n- Error logged and returned to proxy\n- Other proxies unaffected\n- Investigation via logs\n\n---\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n### 1. Immutable PushContext\n\nEach push uses a snapshot of configuration. Prevents races where:\n- Generator reads a value\n- Configuration changes\n- Generator reads different value mid-operation\n\n### 2. Debounced Pushes\n\nMultiple rapid changes are debounced to:\n- Reduce computational load\n- Reduce network overhead\n- Ensure configuration converges before pushing\n\nTunable via `DebounceAfter` and `debounceMax` flags.\n\n### 3. Per-Proxy Generators\n\nEach proxy can use a different generator (sidecar vs. gateway vs. waypoint). Allows:\n- Customized config per proxy type\n- External systems to provide custom generators\n\n### 4. Cache-Aware Push Times\n\nPushes include `LastPushTime` to help the xDS cache distinguish stale entries from fresh ones. Ensures cache coherency across pushes.\n\n### 5. Incremental EDS\n\nEDS is incremental (only changed endpoints) while other resources are full. Reduces bandwidth for frequently-changing endpoints without complexity.\n\n---\n\n## Metrics and Observability\n\n### Key Metrics\n\n- **`pilot_xds_pushed_and_acked_configs`** — Configs successfully pushed and acknowledged\n- **`pilot_xds_pushes`** — Total push operations\n- **`pilot_xds_internal_errors`** — Push generation failures\n- **`pilot_xds_cds_latency`**, **`pilot_xds_lds_latency`**, etc. — Resource generation latencies\n- **`pilot_k8s_endpoints_pending_pod`** — Endpoints waiting for pod info (health check indicator)\n- **`pilot_build_push_time`** — Time to build full config (PushContext + resource generation)\n\n### Debug Endpoints\n\n- **`/debug/push_status`** — Per-proxy push status and errors\n- **`/debug/adsz`** — Connected proxy details\n- **`/debug/cdsz`, `/debug_rdsz`, etc.** — Dump generated resources for debugging\n\n---\n\n## Relevant Source Files\n\n### Core Discovery Service\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`** — DiscoveryServer, Push mechanism, Debouncing\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`** — ADS stream handler, Connection lifecycle, processRequest()\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go`** — Delta XDS (incremental) support\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/pushqueue.go`** — Push queue and throttling\n\n### Resource Generators\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/cds.go`** — Cluster Discovery Service generator\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/lds.go`** — Listener Discovery Service generator\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/rds.go`** — Route Discovery Service generator\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`** — Endpoint Discovery Service generator\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/sds.go`** — Secrets Discovery Service generator\n\n### Configuration and Routing\n- **`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`** — PushContext, Indexes, Configuration snapshot\n- **`pilot/pkg/model/context.go`** — **`pilot/pkg/networking/core/envoyfilter/`** — EnvoyFilter patch application\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/filters/`** — XDS filter implementations\n\n### Tests\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/ads_test.go`** — ADS stream and connection tests\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/cds_test.go`**, **`rds_test.go`**, **`eds_test.go`**, etc. — Per-resource-type tests\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/adstest.go`** — Testing utilities for XDS interactions\n- **`pilot/pkg/model/push_context_test.go`** — PushContext tests\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nIstio's Discovery Service implements a sophisticated control plane that:\n\n1. **Maintains consistency** via immutable PushContext snapshots\n2. **Scales efficiently** via debounced pushes, caching, and incremental updates\n3. **Supports extensibility** via pluggable generators, registries, and EnvoyFilters\n4. **Handles complexity** of multi-cluster deployments, service visibility rules, and Sidecar scopes\n5. **Provides observability** via metrics, debug endpoints, and per-proxy status tracking\n\nThe four subsystems work together: **DiscoveryServer** receives configuration changes and manages the fleet, **ADS** establishes individual proxy connections, **PushContext** provides a consistent view of the mesh configuration, and **ServiceRegistry** feeds service discovery information. This architecture allows thousands of proxies to receive real-time configuration updates while maintaining correctness and efficiency.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3131,"cache_read_input_tokens":49698,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3131},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"81c4d99d-731d-4788-aebf-2a01b857f066","uuid":"b5af1766-7b41-4528-89da-29faf11f35d2"}

It serves a bidirectional gRPC stream to each connected proxy, allowing Pilot to push configuration updates in real-time while proxies request specific resources. The service integrates with multiple service registries (Kubernetes, ServiceEntry, external services), supports multi-cluster deployments, and efficiently manages thousands of concurrent proxy connections.\n\nThis document explains the four primary subsystems that work together to implement this functionality:\n\n1. **DiscoveryServer** — The gRPC server implementing Envoy's xDS v3 protocol\n2. **ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service)** — The bidirectional stream handler and connection model\n3. **PushContext** — The immutable configuration snapshot used during each push\n4. **ServiceRegistry** — The service discovery layer feeding the DiscoveryServer\n\n---\n\n## 1. DiscoveryServer — The xDS gRPC Server\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe `DiscoveryServer` (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:64`) is the central gRPC service that implements Envoy's xDS v3 protocol. It manages all active proxy connections, coordinates configuration pushes across the fleet, implements request-rate limiting, and maintains caches of generated xDS resources.\n\n### Architecture\n\n**Core Fields** (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:65-138`):\n\n- **`Env *model.Environment`** — The cluster's configuration state, including:\n  - `ServiceDiscovery` — The service registry interface\n  - `ConfigStore` — Istio's CRD store (VirtualServices, DestinationRules, etc.)\n  - `Cache` — The xDS resource cache\n  - `pushContext` — The current mesh-wide configuration snapshot\n\n- **`adsClients map[string]*Connection`** — Tracks all active proxy connections, keyed by proxy ID. Each connection wraps a bidirectional gRPC stream with proxy metadata. This map is the single source of truth for which proxies are connected.\n\n- **`Generators map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator`** — Maps generator types to custom implementations. Users extend Pilot by registering custom generators for resource types. Each generator implements the `XdsResourceGenerator` interface to produce resource-specific outputs (Clusters, Listeners, Routes, etc.).\n\n- **`pushChannel chan *model.PushRequest`** — A buffered channel (size 10) that debounces rapid configuration changes. When a config event arrives (e.g., ServiceEntry created, VirtualService modified), it's sent to this channel.\n\n- **`pushQueue *PushQueue`** — A queue that accepts debounced push requests and distributes them to proxies. Provides throttling via `concurrentPushLimit`.\n\n- **`concurrentPushLimit chan struct{}`** — A semaphore (size controlled by `PushThrottle` feature flag) that limits concurrent xDS pushes to prevent overwhelming the system.\n\n- **`RequestRateLimit *rate.Limiter`** — Per-request rate limiting to prevent thundering herd of incoming requests from proxies.\n\n- **`Cache model.XdsCache`** — Stores computed xDS resources (clusters, listeners, routes, secrets). Can be disabled if caching is not desired.\n\n### Request Processing Pipeline\n\n#### 1. **Initialization and Registration**\n\nWhen Pilot starts, `NewDiscoveryServer()` (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:141`) creates a `DiscoveryServer` and initializes:\n\n- Empty `adsClients` map for tracking connections\n- Debounce channels and push queues\n- Configuration watchers for config and service registry changes\n\nThe server registers itself with the gRPC server via `Register()` (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:197`), which calls:\n```go\ndiscovery.RegisterAggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer(rpcs, s)\n```\n\n#### 2. **Push Triggering and Debouncing**\n\nWhen any Istio configuration or service registry state changes:\n\n1. **`ConfigUpdate()`** (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`, line 276) is called with a `PushRequest` containing:\n   - `Full bool` — Whether to recompute the entire push context\n   - `ConfigsUpdated sets.Set[ConfigKey]` — Specific configurations that changed (optimization)\n   - `Reason ReasonStats` — Debugging reason (e.g., \"ServiceEntryCreated\", \"EndpointsUpdated\")\n\n2. The request enters `pushChannel` for debouncing in `handleUpdates()` (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:326`), which:\n   - Waits for a quiet period (`DebounceAfter`) without new changes\n   - Coalesces multiple changes into a single push\n   - Enforces maximum wait time (`debounceMax`)\n\n3. **`Push()`** (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:258`) is called with the debounced request:\n   - If full push, `initPushContext()` recomputes the entire mesh state\n   - Updates `CommittedUpdates` counter\n   - Enqueues the request in `pushQueue` for distribution to proxies\n\n#### 3. **Cache Management**\n\nThe `Cache` field implements the `model.XdsCache` interface, storing computed resources keyed by:\n- Proxy metadata (region, cluster, node type)\n- Resource type (Cluster, Listener, Route, etc.)\n- Configuration version\n\n**Cache Invalidation** (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:246`):\n- `dropCacheForRequest()` clears the cache when configuration changes\n- If a push is `Full`, the entire cache is cleared\n- If incremental, only affected resource types are invalidated\n\n---\n\n## 2. ADS and the Connection Model\n\n### Overview\n\nThe Aggregated Discovery Service (ADS) in `ads.go` implements the bidirectional gRPC streaming protocol that connects Pilot to Envoy proxies. A single `Stream()` handler manages the lifecycle of each proxy connection and coordinates configuration push/pull interactions.\n\n### Connection Lifecycle\n\n#### The `Connection` Type (`pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go:71-88`)\n\nEach connected proxy is represented by a `Connection` struct:\n\n```go\ntype Connection struct {\n    xds.Connection           // Embedded base with stream and peer address\n    node *core.Node          // Original Envoy node metadata\n    proxy *model.Proxy       // Parsed proxy metadata (cluster, namespace, etc.)\n    deltaStream ...          // For Delta XDS (incremental)\n    s *DiscoveryServer       // Reference to parent server\n    ids []string             // Identity certificates from mTLS\n}\n```\n\nKey responsibilities:\n- **Wraps the gRPC stream** — Holds the `DiscoveryStream` for bidirectional communication\n- **Stores proxy metadata** — Extracts and caches information from Envoy's node metadata (cluster ID, pod name, namespace, etc.)\n- **Tracks state** — Maintains resource versions, watched resources, and last push time\n\n#### Establishing a Connection: `Stream()` (`pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go:188-235`)\n\n1. **Server Readiness Check** — Returns `Unavailable` if caches not synced; prevents connecting proxies from getting empty config\n2. **Authentication** (`ads.go:220-228`) — Validates mTLS/authentication credentials\n3. **Rate Limiting** (`ads.go:215`) — Enforces per-request rate limit using token bucket\n4. **Context Initialization** (`ads.go:231`):\n   ```go\n   s.globalPushContext().InitContext(s.Env, nil, nil)\n   ```\n   This ensures the global push context is populated. Happens once; subsequent calls return immediately.\n5. **Connection Creation** (`ads.go:232-234`):\n   - Creates a new `Connection` struct wrapping the stream\n   - Sets parent reference `con.s = s`\n   - Delegates to `xds.Stream()` for stream handling\n6. **Proxy Initialization** in `initConnection()` (`ads.go:240`):\n   - Parses node metadata into a `Proxy` object\n   - Registers the connection in `adsClients` map\n   - Initializes proxy-specific state (sidecar scope, watched resources)\n\n### Request Processing: `processRequest()` (`ads.go:139-181`)\n\nWhen an Envoy proxy sends a `DiscoveryRequest`:\n\n1. **Deduplication Check** — `xds.ShouldRespond()` determines if a response is needed based on:\n   - Previous version (already sent to this proxy)\n   - Nonce (preventing duplicate ACKs)\n\n2. **Configuration Preparation** — Constructs a `PushRequest` with:\n   - The proxy's last known `PushContext` (to avoid re-initializing)\n   - `Full: true` for immediate response (not waiting for debouncing)\n   - Last push time (used by cache for staleness detection)\n\n3. **Sidecar Scope Validation** (`ads.go:173-179`) — If the proxy's sidecar scope version doesn't match the push context version, `computeProxyState()` recomputes it\n\n4. **Response Generation** — Calls `pushXds()` to generate and send the response via the appropriate generator\n\n### Push Coordination: `pushConnection()` (`ads.go`, line not shown but referenced)\n\nWhen Pilot needs to push configuration to a specific connection:\n\n1. Gets the `Generator` for the proxy type (sidecar, gateway, waypoint)\n2. Calls `Generator.Generate()` to produce xDS resources for the proxy\n3. Sends a `DiscoveryResponse` via the stream\n4. Updates metrics and error tracking\n\n### Delta XDS: `DeltaAggregatedResources()` (`ads.go:467`)\n\nFor incremental updates, Envoy can use Delta XDS to receive only changed resources:\n\n1. **Incremental Resources** — Only resources that changed are sent\n2. **Deleted Resources** — Resource names that should be removed are sent\n3. **State Tracking** — The client tracks subscribed resources and version numbers\n\nThis reduces bandwidth for large clusters with frequent endpoint updates.\n\n---\n\n## 3. PushContext — Configuration Snapshot and Translation\n\n### Purpose\n\nA `PushContext` is an **immutable snapshot of the entire mesh configuration** used during a single push. It's created when configuration changes and shared across all proxies during that push, ensuring consistency. It also serves as the translation engine that converts Istio's high-level configuration into Envoy-specific resources.\n\nLocated in: `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:207-280`\n\n### Architecture\n\n#### Core Indexes\n\nA `PushContext` maintains several in-memory indexes for fast lookups:\n\n1. **`ServiceIndex serviceIndex`** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:65-91`) — Indexes all services by visibility:\n   - `public` — Services with `exportTo: \"*\"` (visible across the mesh)\n   - `privateByNamespace` — Services with `exportTo: \".\"` (visible only within namespace)\n   - `exportedToNamespace` — Services exported to specific namespaces\n   - `HostnameAndNamespace` — Services keyed by hostname and namespace\n   - `instancesByPort` — Cached endpoint lookups by port\n\n   **Usage**: When generating CDS (Cluster Discovery Service), Pilot looks up services this index determines which proxies can see which services.\n\n2. **`virtualServiceIndex virtualServiceIndex`** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:100-116`) — Indexes VirtualServices by visibility:\n   - `publicByGateway` — Public VirtualServices by gateway\n   - `privateByNamespaceAndGateway` — Namespace-local VirtualServices\n   - `delegates` — Delegates in VirtualService hierarchies\n   - `referencedDestinations` — Services referenced by VirtualServices\n\n   **Usage**: When generating RDS (Route Discovery Service), Pilot looks up VirtualServices to build HTTP routes.\n\n3. **`destinationRuleIndex destinationRuleIndex`** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:132-146`) — Indexes DestinationRules:\n   - `namespaceLocal` — DestinationRules per namespace\n   - `exportedByNamespace` — Exported DestinationRules\n   - `specificDestRules` and `wildcardDestRules` — Organized by target host\n\n   **Usage**: When generating clusters, DestinationRules are consulted for load balancing policies, connection pools, and traffic policies.\n\n4. **`sidecarIndex sidecarIndex`** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:148-180`) — Stores Sidecar configurations:\n   - `sidecarsByNamespace` — User-defined sidecars per namespace\n   - `meshRootSidecarConfig` — Root namespace sidecar (defaults for whole mesh)\n   - `defaultSidecarsByNamespace` — Computed defaults if no sidecar defined\n\n   **Usage**: Sidecars define which services a proxy can see. When computing routes and clusters for a proxy, the sidecar scope limits what's included.\n\n5. **`gatewayIndex gatewayIndex`** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:182-195`) — Indexes Gateway resources by namespace and globally.\n\n6. **`virtualServiceIndex.delegates`** — Maps root VirtualServices to their delegates, used for hierarchical route computation.\n\n#### Metrics and Status Tracking\n\n- **`ProxyStatus map[string]map[string]ProxyPushStatus`** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:211`) — Tracks push errors per proxy per error code, used for debugging and metrics\n- **`serviceAccounts map[serviceAccountKey][]string`** — Maps services to their service accounts for RBAC\n\n#### Configuration Objects\n\nA `PushContext` also holds:\n\n- **`Mesh *meshconfig.MeshConfig`** — Global mesh configuration\n- **`JwtKeyResolver *model.JwksResolver`** — JWT public key resolver for authentication policies\n- **`AuthnPolicies *AuthenticationPolicies`** — Authentication policies in the mesh\n- **`AuthzPolicies *AuthorizationPolicies`** — Authorization (RBAC) policies\n- **`Telemetry *Telemetries`** — Telemetry policies\n- **`ProxyConfigs *ProxyConfigs`** — Per-proxy configuration overrides\n- **`Networks *meshconfig.MeshNetworks`** — Multi-cluster network topology\n\n### PushContext Lifecycle\n\n#### Creation: `NewPushContext()` (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:735`)\n\nCreates a new, empty `PushContext` with initialized but empty indexes.\n\n#### Initialization: `InitContext()` (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`, method)\n\nCalled when configuration changes to populate the indexes:\n\n1. **Rebuilds all indexes** from the current `ConfigStore`:\n   - Scans all Services and builds `ServiceIndex`\n   - Scans all VirtualServices and builds `virtualServiceIndex`\n   - Scans all DestinationRules and indexes them\n   - Indexes Sidecars, Gateways, EnvoyFilters, etc.\n\n2. **Applies visibility rules** based on `exportTo`:\n   - Services/routing rules with `exportTo: \"*\"` go into `public`\n   - `exportTo: \".\"` goes into `privateByNamespace`\n   - Explicit namespace exports are indexed separately\n\n3. **Computes derived state**:\n   - Merges DestinationRules for the same host\n   - Validates configurations and logs errors\n   - Caches endpoint lookups for frequently accessed services\n\n4. **Thread-safety**: Protected by `initializeMutex`; multiple concurrent calls return immediately after first initialization\n\n**Performance Note**: `InitContext()` is expensive (scans all CRDs, indexes them) and happens only when configuration changes (debounced). This is why it's debounced; calling it on every request would be prohibitively expensive.\n\n### Configuration Translation: From Istio to Envoy\n\nThe `PushContext` serves as the input to resource generators that translate Istio's configuration into Envoy resources. The translation happens in `pilot/pkg/networking/core/` and uses the indexes in `PushContext`.\n\n#### Example: VirtualService → Route\n\n1. **Input**: A `VirtualService` specifying:\n   ```yaml\n   apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3\n   kind: VirtualService\n   metadata:\n     name: bookinfo\n   spec:\n     hosts:\n     - bookinfo.example.com\n     http:\n     - match:\n       - uri:\n           prefix: /reviews\n       route:\n       - destination:\n           host: reviews\n           port:\n             number: 8080\n           subset: v1\n   ```\n\n2. **Generator Lookup**:\n   - RDS generator (`pilot/pkg/xds/rds.go`) is invoked for the requesting proxy\n   - Looks up `bookinfo.example.com` in `virtualServiceIndex.publicByGateway`\n   - Retrieves the `VirtualService` spec\n\n3. **Route Computation** (`pilot/pkg/networking/core/route/`):\n   - Builds an Envoy `RouteConfiguration` with:\n     - Route match conditions (URI prefix)\n     - Route actions (forward to `reviews` cluster)\n     - Weights, retries, timeouts from the VirtualService spec\n\n4. **DestinationRule Application**:\n   - Looks up `reviews` in `destinationRuleIndex`\n   - If a `DestinationRule` exists for `reviews`, applies:\n     - Load balancing policy (round-robin, least request, etc.)\n     - Connection pool settings\n     - Outlier detection\n\n5. **Output**: An Envoy `RouteConfiguration` with fully populated route actions\n\n#### Example: Service + DestinationRule → Cluster\n\n1. **Input**: A Kubernetes Service `reviews.default.svc.cluster.local` and optional `DestinationRule`\n\n2. **Cluster Generation** (`pilot/pkg/xds/cds.go`, `pilot/pkg/networking/core/cluster_builder.go`):\n   - Looks up the service in `ServiceIndex.public` or `privateByNamespace`\n   - Creates an Envoy Cluster with:\n     - Service name as cluster name\n     - Virtual IP (from ClusterVIPs) or DNS resolution mode\n     - Service ports\n\n3. **DestinationRule Enhancements**:\n   - Looks up `DestinationRule` for the service in `destinationRuleIndex`\n   - If subsets are defined, creates subset-specific clusters (e.g., `reviews-v1`, `reviews-v2`)\n   - Applies load balancing, connection pools, outlier detection\n\n4. **Endpoint Resolution** (EDS — Endpoint Discovery Service):\n   - **Full CDS**: Cluster points to EDS (dynamic endpoint discovery)\n   - **EDS**: Endpoints are fetched from service registry, filtered by:\n     - Health status (Ready pods only)\n     - Sidecar scope visibility\n     - Network locality (for multi-cluster routing)\n\n### Shared State During Push\n\nDuring a single push:\n- All proxies see the same `PushContext` snapshot\n- All resource generators use the same indexes\n- If config changes mid-push, they're debounced and handled in the next push\n\nThis guarantees **consistency** — a proxy won't receive partially updated configuration that doesn't match other proxies' views.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe service registry feeds the discovery service with information about available services and their endpoints. It's abstracted via the `ServiceDiscovery` interface (`pilot/pkg/model/service.go:899`), allowing multiple implementations for Kubernetes, ServiceEntry, external registries, and aggregation across clusters.\n\n### ServiceDiscovery Interface (`pilot/pkg/model/service.go:899`)\n\nThe interface defines:\n\n```go\ntype ServiceDiscovery interface {\n    Services() []*Service\n    GetService(hostname host.Name) *Service\n    GetProxyServiceTargets(proxy *model.Proxy) []model.ServiceTarget\n    InstancesByPort(svc *Service, port int, labels labels.Collection) []*model.IstioEndpoint\n    GetNetworkGateway(network string) *model.NetworkGateway\n    // ... and other methods\n}\n```\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- **`Services()`** — Returns all services in the registry\n- **`GetService(hostname)`** — Looks up a service by FQDN\n- **`InstancesByPort()`** — Gets endpoints for a service on a specific port, optionally filtered by labels\n- **`GetProxyServiceTargets()`** — Returns services co-located with a proxy (for multi-cluster routing)\n\n### Kubernetes Service Registry\n\nThe Kubernetes implementation in `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/` watches Kubernetes API objects:\n\n#### Watched Resources:\n\n1. **Services** (`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go`):\n   - Each Kubernetes Service becomes an Istio Service\n   - Hostname: `<name>.<namespace>.svc.cluster.local`\n   - Ports, ClusterIP, and labels are extracted\n\n2. **EndpointSlices** (`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/endpointslice.go`):\n   - Kubernetes 1.19+ uses EndpointSlices instead of Endpoints\n   - Each slice contains a subset of endpoints for a service\n   - Pilot aggregates slices and watches for changes\n\n3. **Pods** (`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/pod.go`):\n   - Watches pod creation/deletion to track endpoint health\n   - Used for determining which endpoints are \"Ready\"\n   - Feeds into the EndpointIndex for EDS\n\n4. **Nodes** (`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/network.go`):\n   - Watches node labels for region/zone topology\n   - Used for locality-aware load balancing\n\n#### Service Registry Flow:\n\n```\nKubernetes API\n    ↓\nService/Endpoint Watchers\n    ↓\nEndpointIndex (pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go)\n    ↓\nProxyUpdate() [notifies xDS server]\n    ↓\nDiscoveryServer.ConfigUpdate()\n    ↓\nPush to all proxies\n```\n\nWhen a pod is added/removed:\n1. EndpointSlice changes → detected by watcher\n2. `ProxyUpdate()` is called → triggers EDS push\n3. Pilot computes endpoint list and sends EDS update to proxies\n4. Proxies update their load balancers\n\n### ServiceEntry Registry\n\n`ServiceEntry` CRDs allow declaring external services:\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3\nkind: ServiceEntry\nmetadata:\n  name: external-db\nspec:\n  hosts:\n  - db.external.example.com\n  ports:\n  - port: 5432\n    protocol: TCP\n  resolution: STATIC\n  endpoints:\n  - address: 192.168.1.1\n```\n\nThe `serviceentry` registry provider converts these into Istio Service objects, allowing them to be treated like Kubernetes services for routing purposes.\n\n### Aggregate Controller (Multi-Cluster)\n\nThe aggregate controller in `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/` combines multiple service registries:\n\n```\nKubernetes Cluster 1\n    ↓\nKubernetes Registry\n    ↓\n        → Aggregate Controller → Combined view\n        ↓\nKubernetes Cluster 2\n    ↓\nKubernetes Registry + ServiceEntry\n```\n\n**Multi-Cluster Logic**:\n\n1. **Local Services** — From the local cluster's Kubernetes registry\n2. **Remote Services** — From other clusters (via `ServiceImport` CRDs or direct watches)\n3. **ServiceEntry Services** — Defined via Istio CRDs\n\nAll are aggregated into a single `ServiceDiscovery` interface. A proxy in Cluster 1 can access services from Cluster 2 if they're exported via:\n- Kubernetes `ServiceExport` CRD\n- Istio `exportTo` rules\n- Multi-cluster networking configuration\n\n#### Cross-Cluster Routing:\n\nWhen a proxy in Cluster 1 needs to reach a service in Cluster 2:\n\n1. Service discovered via aggregate registry (Cluster 2's service)\n2. CDS includes endpoints from Cluster 2\n3. Endpoints include the cross-cluster gateway IP (from `NetworkManager`)\n4. Traffic is routed through the gateway (via mTLS or HBONE in ambient mode)\n\n### Endpoint Index: Efficient Endpoint Lookups\n\nThe `EndpointIndex` in `pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go` maintains efficient endpoint lookups:\n\n- **Organized by Service Key** — `namespace/hostname`\n- **Sharded by Endpoint IP** — Allows for incremental updates (when pod scales, only affected shard updates)\n- **Cached InstancesByPort Results** — Frequently accessed endpoint lookups are cached\n\n**Usage in EDS**:\n\n```\nEDS Request (what endpoints for service X?)\n    ↓\nEndpointIndex.InstancesByPort(service X, port 8080)\n    ↓\nReturns endpoints filtered by:\n   - Health status (Ready pods only)\n   - Labels (if specified in DestinationRule subset)\n   - Network locality (for locality-aware load balancing)\n```\n\n### Triggering Pushes from Service Registry\n\nWhen service state changes:\n\n1. **Endpoint Change** (pod added/removed):\n   - Triggers EDS (Endpoint Discovery Service) push (not full push)\n   - Reason: `EndpointUpdate`\n   - Only clusters referencing that service are updated\n\n2. **Service Change** (service created/deleted):\n   - Triggers full CDS (Cluster Discovery Service) push\n   - Also triggers LDS/RDS (listeners and routes may reference new service)\n   - Reason: `ServiceUpdate`\n\n3. **Debouncing**:\n   - Multiple endpoint changes are debounced (if `EnableEDSDebounce` is true)\n   - Avoids flapping when many pods scale simultaneously\n\n### Multi-Cluster Failure Handling\n\nIf a remote cluster becomes unavailable:\n\n1. **Service discovery removes remote services** from the aggregate view\n2. **Proxies are updated** via a config push\n3. **Routes referencing removed services** are pruned\n4. **Clients get connection errors** (graceful degradation)\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: From Configuration Change to Proxy Update\n\n### Complete Example: VirtualService Creation\n\n```\n1. User creates VirtualService CRD in Kubernetes\n   ↓\n2. Kubernetes API notifies ConfigStore watcher\n   ↓\n3. ConfigStore calls ConfigUpdate() with:\n   {Full: true, ConfigsUpdated: {VirtualService/namespace/name}, Reason: ConfigUpdate}\n   ↓\n4. ConfigUpdate() sends to pushChannel\n   ↓\n5. handleUpdates() debounces (waits for quiet period or max delay)\n   ↓\n6. Push() is called:\n   a. initPushContext() rescans all CRDs, rebuilds indexes\n   b. Calls computeProxyState() for each connected proxy (if needed)\n   c. Enqueues PushRequest in pushQueue\n   ↓\n7. sendPushes() distributes:\n   a. Acquires concurrentPushLimit semaphore\n   b. Iterates over adsClients (all connected proxies)\n   c. For each proxy, calls pushConnection()\n   ↓\n8. For each proxy, resource generators create Envoy config:\n   a. RDS generator uses virtualServiceIndex to build routes\n   b. CDS generator uses ServiceIndex to build clusters\n   c. Generators apply DestinationRules, EnvoyFilters, etc.\n   ↓\n9. xDS responses are sent to proxies via gRPC stream\n   ↓\n10. Proxies acknowledge with DiscoveryRequest (ACK/NACK)\n    ↓\n11. Errors tracked in ProxyStatus for debugging\n```\n\n### Complete Example: Pod Scale Event\n\n```\n1. Pod is added in Kubernetes\n   ↓\n2. EndpointSlice watcher detects change\n   ↓\n3. EndpointIndex is updated with new endpoint IP\n   ↓\n4. EndpointIndex calls ProxyUpdate() via callback\n   ↓\n5. ProxyUpdate() calls ConfigUpdate() with:\n   {Full: false, Reason: EndpointUpdate}\n   ↓\n6. (Same debounce → push → xDS flow)\n   ↓\n7. EDS generator reads EndpointIndex for affected service\n   ↓\n8. EDS update sent to proxies referencing the service\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\n### 1. Custom Resource Generators\n\nUsers can extend Istio by registering custom generators for any xDS resource type:\n\n```go\ngenerator := &myCustomGenerator{}\ndiscoveryServer.Generators[\"my-generator-type\"] = generator\n```\n\nGenerators implement the `XdsResourceGenerator` interface:\n- `Generate()` — Called to produce resources for a proxy\n- `GenerateDelta()` — Called for delta/incremental updates\n\n**Use Cases**:\n- Custom cluster discovery from external systems\n- Custom route generation based on external rules\n- Custom secret generation from external PKI\n\n### 2. Custom Configuration Types\n\nVia the `ConfigStore` interface, custom CRD types can be added. Pilot will:\n- Watch the new type\n- Include it in `InitContext()` rebuilding\n- Trigger pushes when instances change\n\n**Use Cases**:\n- Custom traffic policies\n- Custom observability configurations\n- Custom security rules\n\n### 3. EnvoyFilter\n\nEnvoyFilter CRDs in `pilot/pkg/networking/core/envoyfilter/` allow patching generated Envoy config:\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3\nkind: EnvoyFilter\nmetadata:\n  name: add-custom-header\nspec:\n  workloadSelector:\n    labels:\n      app: httpbin\n  configPatches:\n  - applyTo: HTTP_FILTER\n    patch:\n      operation: INSERT_BEFORE\n      value:\n        name: custom-header-filter\n        typed_config:\n          \"@type\": ...\n```\n\nEnvoyFilters are indexed in `PushContext.envoyFiltersByNamespace` and applied during resource generation.\n\n### 4. External Service Registries\n\nCustom `ServiceDiscovery` implementations can be registered:\n\n```go\ncustomRegistry := NewCustomServiceRegistry()\naggregate.Controller.AddRegistry(customRegistry)\n```\n\nAllows integrating with:\n- Consul\n- Eureka\n- Custom APIs\n- Cloud provider service catalogs\n\n### 5. Request Hooks\n\nProxyNeedsPush (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go:78`) allows filtering which proxies get pushed:\n\n```go\ndiscoveryServer.ProxyNeedsPush = func(proxy *model.Proxy, req *model.PushRequest) (*model.PushRequest, bool) {\n    if shouldSkip(proxy) {\n        return nil, false  // Skip this proxy\n    }\n    return req, true\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases**:\n- Route updates only to affected proxies\n- Skip proxies in specific conditions\n- Custom push logic\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### 1. Configuration Validation Errors\n\nWhen `InitContext()` processes configurations:\n- Invalid CRDs are logged, not propagated\n- `PushContext.ProxyStatus` tracks errors per proxy\n- Proxies continue with last-known-good configuration\n\n**Recovery**: Fix the CRD and push again.\n\n### 2. Push Failures\n\nIf an error occurs while pushing to a proxy:\n- Tracked in `ProxyStatus[proxyID][errorCode]`\n- Exposed via `/debug/push_status` endpoint\n- Next `ConfigUpdate()` will retry\n\n**Common causes**:\n- Network errors (transient)\n- Stream closed (proxy disconnected)\n- Resource generation failure (bug)\n\n### 3. Proxy Connection Failures\n\nIf a proxy disconnects:\n- Connection is removed from `adsClients`\n- Next connection reconnects and gets full config\n- No special recovery needed\n\n### 4. Resource Generation Panics\n\nGenerators that panic are caught:\n- Error logged and returned to proxy\n- Other proxies unaffected\n- Investigation via logs\n\n---\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n### 1. Immutable PushContext\n\nEach push uses a snapshot of configuration. Prevents races where:\n- Generator reads a value\n- Configuration changes\n- Generator reads different value mid-operation\n\n### 2. Debounced Pushes\n\nMultiple rapid changes are debounced to:\n- Reduce computational load\n- Reduce network overhead\n- Ensure configuration converges before pushing\n\nTunable via `DebounceAfter` and `debounceMax` flags.\n\n### 3. Per-Proxy Generators\n\nEach proxy can use a different generator (sidecar vs. gateway vs. waypoint). Allows:\n- Customized config per proxy type\n- External systems to provide custom generators\n\n### 4. Cache-Aware Push Times\n\nPushes include `LastPushTime` to help the xDS cache distinguish stale entries from fresh ones. Ensures cache coherency across pushes.\n\n### 5. Incremental EDS\n\nEDS is incremental (only changed endpoints) while other resources are full. Reduces bandwidth for frequently-changing endpoints without complexity.\n\n---\n\n## Metrics and Observability\n\n### Key Metrics\n\n- **`pilot_xds_pushed_and_acked_configs`** — Configs successfully pushed and acknowledged\n- **`pilot_xds_pushes`** — Total push operations\n- **`pilot_xds_internal_errors`** — Push generation failures\n- **`pilot_xds_cds_latency`**, **`pilot_xds_lds_latency`**, etc. — Resource generation latencies\n- **`pilot_k8s_endpoints_pending_pod`** — Endpoints waiting for pod info (health check indicator)\n- **`pilot_build_push_time`** — Time to build full config (PushContext + resource generation)\n\n### Debug Endpoints\n\n- **`/debug/push_status`** — Per-proxy push status and errors\n- **`/debug/adsz`** — Connected proxy details\n- **`/debug/cdsz`, `/debug_rdsz`, etc.** — Dump generated resources for debugging\n\n---\n\n## Relevant Source Files\n\n### Core Discovery Service\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`** — DiscoveryServer, Push mechanism, Debouncing\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`** — ADS stream handler, Connection lifecycle, processRequest()\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go`** — Delta XDS (incremental) support\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/pushqueue.go`** — Push queue and throttling\n\n### Resource Generators\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/cds.go`** — Cluster Discovery Service generator\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/lds.go`** — Listener Discovery Service generator\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/rds.go`** — Route Discovery Service generator\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`** — Endpoint Discovery Service generator\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/sds.go`** — Secrets Discovery Service generator\n\n### Configuration and Routing\n- **`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`** — PushContext, Indexes, Configuration snapshot\n- **`pilot/pkg/model/context.go`** — Environment, Proxy metadata\n- **`pilot/pkg/model/service.go`** — Service model, ServiceDiscovery interface\n- **`pilot/pkg/networking/core/configgen.go`** — ConfigGenerator interface\n- **`pilot/pkg/networking/core/cluster_builder.go`** — Cluster resource building\n- **`pilot/pkg/networking/core/listener_builder.go`** — Listener resource building\n- **`pilot/pkg/networking/core/route/`** — HTTP route generation from VirtualServices\n\n### Service Registry\n- **`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go`** — Kubernetes service watcher\n- **`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/endpointslice.go`** — Endpoint watching\n- **`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go`** — Multi-registry aggregation\n- **`pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go`** — Efficient endpoint lookups\n- **`pilot/pkg/model/service.go`** — Service model\n\n### EnvoyFilter and Extensions\n- **`pilot/pkg/networking/core/envoyfilter/`** — EnvoyFilter patch application\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/filters/`** — XDS filter implementations\n\n### Tests\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/ads_test.go`** — ADS stream and connection tests\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/cds_test.go`**, **`rds_test.go`**, **`eds_test.go`**, etc. — Per-resource-type tests\n- **`pilot/pkg/xds/adstest.go`** — Testing utilities for XDS interactions\n- **`pilot/pkg/model/push_context_test.go`** — PushContext tests\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nIstio's Discovery Service implements a sophisticated control plane that:\n\n1. **Maintains consistency** via immutable PushContext snapshots\n2. **Scales efficiently** via debounced pushes, caching, and incremental updates\n3. **Supports extensibility** via pluggable generators, registries, and EnvoyFilters\n4. **Handles complexity** of multi-cluster deployments, service visibility rules, and Sidecar scopes\n5. **Provides observability** via metrics, debug endpoints, and per-proxy status tracking\n\nThe four subsystems work together: **DiscoveryServer** receives configuration changes and manages the fleet, **ADS** establishes individual proxy connections, **PushContext** provides a consistent view of the mesh configuration, and **ServiceRegistry** feeds service discovery information. This architecture allows thousands of proxies to receive real-time configuration updates while maintaining correctness and efficiency.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
